scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.agencias.pr.gov/municipio/cayey">www<wbr />.agencias<wbr />.pr<wbr />.gov<wbr />/municipio<wbr />/cayey</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Cayey</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;ka\xcb\x88\xca\x9dej&#93;</a></span>), officially <b>Cayey de Muesas</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Gov_Cayey_Info_Manual_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Gov_Cayey_Info_Manual-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is a mountain <a href="/wiki/Cayey_barrio-pueblo" title="Cayey barrio-pueblo">town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> in central <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> located on the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Cayey" title="Sierra de Cayey">Sierra de Cayey</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Central Mountain range</a>, north of <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Salinas, Puerto Rico">Salinas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guayama,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guayama, Puerto Rico">Guayama</a>; south of <a href="/wiki/Cidra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cidra, Puerto Rico">Cidra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas</a>; east of <a href="/wiki/Aibonito,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aibonito, Puerto Rico">Aibonito</a> and Salinas; and west of <a href="/wiki/San_Lorenzo,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Lorenzo, Puerto Rico">San Lorenzo</a>. Cayey is spread over 21 barrios plus <a href="/wiki/Cayey_barrio-pueblo" title="Cayey barrio-pueblo">Cayey Pueblo</a> (the downtown area and the administrative center). It is part of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area">San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area</a>.\n</p><p>Cayey is notable for its surrounding mountains. The city has been actively growing since the 1990s, evidenced by its designation as a <a href="/wiki/San_Juan%E2%80%93Caguas%E2%80%93Guaynabo_metropolitan_area" title="San Juan\xe2\x80\x93Caguas\xe2\x80\x93Guaynabo metropolitan area">Metropolitan Area</a> by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">U.S. Census Bureau</a>. It has experienced significant growth in commerce, and many major retailers, such as <a href="/wiki/Wal-Mart" class="mw-redirect" title="Wal-Mart">Wal-Mart</a> have opened stores in the city. Industries in Cayey include sugar, tobacco and poultry. For tobacco there is a well-known company called Consolidated Cigar Corp.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A new coliseum and hospital facilities have also been built. <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> is a major corporation that has a manufacturing facility in the town. Cayey is also host to one of the campuses of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="University of Puerto Rico">University of Puerto Rico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Cayey" title="University of Puerto Rico at Cayey">University of Puerto Rico at Cayey</a>.\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cayey_-_Street_Scene_(1906).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Cayey_-_Street_Scene_%281906%29.jpg/220px-Cayey_-_Street_Scene_%281906%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Cayey_-_Street_Scene_%281906%29.jpg/330px-Cayey_-_Street_Scene_%281906%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Cayey_-_Street_Scene_%281906%29.jpg/440px-Cayey_-_Street_Scene_%281906%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1360" data-file-height="879" /></a><figcaption>Street scene in Cayey in 1906</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Cayey was founded on August 17, 1773, by Juan Mata V\xc3\xa1zquez, who became its first mayor. It is popularly said that Cayey derives its name from the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Ta\xc3\xadno language">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> word for "a place of waters". It was named <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Cayey de Muesas</i></span> in honor of <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miguel_de_Muesas" class="extiw" title="es:Miguel de Muesas">Miguel de Muesas</a>, the then governor of Puerto Rico. The town is located in a valley nestled between Puerto Rico\'s <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a> mountain range and the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Cayey" title="Sierra de Cayey">Sierra de Cayey</a> at roughly the midpoint of routes <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_1" title="Puerto Rico Highway 1">PR-1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_52" title="Puerto Rico Highway 52">PR-52</a>. The routes lead to a popular drive that provides panoramic views of the island from its highest points.\n</p><p>Puerto Rico was ceded by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_of_1898" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Paris of 1898">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a> and became a territory of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. In 1899, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_War" title="United States Department of War">United States Department of War</a> conducted a <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> of Puerto Rico finding that the population of Cayey was 14,442.<sup id="cite_ref-OfficeSanger1900_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OfficeSanger1900-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>An education base began in the early to mid-1950s when the <a href="/wiki/Interamerican_University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Interamerican University of Puerto Rico">Interamerican University</a> opened a branch in Cayey providing teacher training through a night class scheme. In 1967 the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="University of Puerto Rico">University of Puerto Rico</a> opened a campus in the former <a href="/wiki/Henry_Barracks,_Puerto_Rico" title="Henry Barracks, Puerto Rico">Henry Barracks</a> Military Reservation, and in the early 1980s <a href="/wiki/Universidad_del_Turabo" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad del Turabo">El Turabo University</a>, subsidiary of the Ana G. Mendez conglomerate opened a campus in the old tobacco factory at the entrance of town. The Interamerican University will be opening a Graduate campus in front of the main town square (<a href="/wiki/Cayey_barrio-pueblo" title="Cayey barrio-pueblo">downtown</a>), and there are conversations with a foreign educational concern to open a technology campus using the buildings left over by the Gordonshire Knitting Mills. There are three major private schools: Radians School, the long established Colegio de Nuestra Senora de la Merced and La Milagrosa School. Cayey\'s health care base expanded in the mid-1960s with the <a href="/wiki/Mennonites" title="Mennonites">Mennonite</a> Medical Center and a Municipal\nHospital along with laboratories, and urgent care centers that cater to the poor and the elderly.\n</p><p>With the construction of the Interstate (<a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_52" title="Puerto Rico Highway 52">PR-52</a>), Cayey has evolved into a "<a href="/wiki/Bedroom_community" class="mw-redirect" title="Bedroom community">bedroom community</a>" with gated housing developments, located just 30 minutes away from <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> and 45 minutes away from <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a>. With pleasant weather and good private schools, Cayey has become a premium location for the affluent.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> on September 20, 2017, triggered numerous landslides in Cayey with significant amount of rain and wind.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The hurricane destroyed 3,000 homes in Cayey.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Rico_National_Guard_(37420248312).jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="National Guard in Cayey after Hurricane Maria"><img alt="National Guard in Cayey after Hurricane Maria" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Puerto_Rico_National_Guard_%2837420248312%29.jpg/120px-Puerto_Rico_National_Guard_%2837420248312%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="80" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Puerto_Rico_National_Guard_%2837420248312%29.jpg/180px-Puerto_Rico_National_Guard_%2837420248312%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Puerto_Rico_National_Guard_%2837420248312%29.jpg/240px-Puerto_Rico_National_Guard_%2837420248312%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1359" /></a></span></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">National Guard in Cayey after Hurricane Maria</div>\n\t\t</li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Lt._Colin_A._Roberts_speaks_with_local_civilian_employees_during_an_assessment_of_Centro_Medico_Menonita_de_Cayey_Hospital%E2%80%99s_medical._(37451604851).jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Mennonite hospital in Cayey"><img alt="Mennonite hospital in Cayey" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Lt._Colin_A._Roberts_speaks_with_local_civilian_employees_during_an_assessment_of_Centro_Medico_Menonita_de_Cayey_Hospital%E2%80%99s_medical._%2837451604851%29.jpg/120px-Lt._Colin_A._Roberts_speaks_with_local_civilian_employees_during_an_assessment_of_Centro_Medico_Menonita_de_Cayey_Hospital%E2%80%99s_medical._%2837451604851%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="80" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Lt._Colin_A._Roberts_speaks_with_local_civilian_employees_during_an_assessment_of_Centro_Medico_Menonita_de_Cayey_Hospital%E2%80%99s_medical._%2837451604851%29.jpg/180px-Lt._Colin_A._Roberts_speaks_with_local_civilian_employees_during_an_assessment_of_Centro_Medico_Menonita_de_Cayey_Hospital%E2%80%99s_medical._%2837451604851%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Lt._Colin_A._Roberts_speaks_with_local_civilian_employees_during_an_assessment_of_Centro_Medico_Menonita_de_Cayey_Hospital%E2%80%99s_medical._%2837451604851%29.jpg/240px-Lt._Colin_A._Roberts_speaks_with_local_civilian_employees_during_an_assessment_of_Centro_Medico_Menonita_de_Cayey_Hospital%E2%80%99s_medical._%2837451604851%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a></span></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">Mennonite hospital in Cayey</div>\n\t\t</li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Damaged_structure_over_a_basketball_court_in_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Damaged basketball court"><img alt="Damaged basketball court" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Damaged_structure_over_a_basketball_court_in_Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/120px-Damaged_structure_over_a_basketball_court_in_Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="84" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Damaged_structure_over_a_basketball_court_in_Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/180px-Damaged_structure_over_a_basketball_court_in_Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Damaged_structure_over_a_basketball_court_in_Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/240px-Damaged_structure_over_a_basketball_court_in_Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="668" /></a></span></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">Damaged basketball court</div>\n\t\t</li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Map of landslides in Puerto Rico"><img alt="Map of landslides in Puerto Rico" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg/120px-Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="89" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg/180px-Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg/240px-Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="770" data-file-height="569" /></a></span></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">Map of landslides in Puerto Rico</div>\n\t\t</li>\n</ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Impact_of_Henry_Barracks_Military_Reservation">Impact of Henry Barracks Military Reservation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Impact of Henry Barracks Military Reservation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Henry_Barracks,_Puerto_Rico" title="Henry Barracks, Puerto Rico">Henry Barracks</a> Military Reservation was a lifeline for the residents of Cayey from 1901 to 1966, when it was declared excess land and passed to the <a href="/wiki/General_Services_Administration" title="General Services Administration">General Services Administration</a> for decommission. The property consisted of 178.03 hectares (439.92 acres)  (<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>). The property was divided into three prominent encampments: the Spanish Camp or Campamento Espa\xc3\xb1ol (6.1 hectares (15 acres) ), Camp Henry or Henry Barracks, the Home of the third Battalion of the <a href="/wiki/65th_Infantry_Regiment" class="mw-redirect" title="65th Infantry Regiment">65th Inf. Regiment</a> that consisted of 151 hectares (372 acres) , and 27 hectares (67 acres)  the Cayey Naval Radio Station (27 hectares (67 acres) )<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>). This reservation is situated in the east of the town of Cayey. The Spanish Reservation containing an area of approximately 6.1 hectares (15 acres) , known as Hospital Hill was set apart by Executive Order of June 30, 1903, under an Act of Congress approved on July 7, 1902.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The main army post was located in the northern part of the reservation, initially housing the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Puerto_Rico_Volunteer_Infantry_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Puerto Rico Volunteer Infantry Regiment (page does not exist)">Puerto Rico Volunteer Infantry Regiment</a>.\n</p><p>The combined posts had approximately 1,200 men who used the resources provided by the town people. Families moved into Punta Brava and Vieques neighborhoods. A laundry, show shop, and other smaller stores were located right outside the gate. By 1906 about 350 civilians had jobs in the two posts (Camp Henry and The Cayey Navy Radio Station).\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Navy" title="United States Department of the Navy">U.S. Department of the Navy</a> submitted a proposal to raise three 190 metres (620&#160;ft)  tall masts as part of a global radio communication linkage. In 1916 the Department of the Navy approved a budget of $40,000. At the time 300 men were hired to build the facility for a period of two-year, the project was completed in 1918<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On September 11, 1928, a category five hurricane called San Felipe destroyed the temporary buildings at Henry Barracks, and the Navy Radio Station.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A radio message was sent from the Cayey Navy Radio Station on September 18, 1928, to follow \xe2\x80\x9cAll buildings Henry Barracks destroyed by hurricane September 13th\xe2\x80\x9d.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\nThe Navy left Cayey and moved its station to Isla Grande and Stop 7 <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1154941027">.mw-parser-output .frac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .frac .num,.mw-parser-output .frac .den{font-size:80%;line-height:0;vertical-align:super}.mw-parser-output .frac .den{vertical-align:sub}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);clip-path:polygon(0px 0px,0px 0px,0px 0px);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="frac"><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">2</span></span> in Puerto de Tierra. All the land held by the Navy included Magazine Hill (known in the community as "El Polvorin"), which was taken over by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">U. S. Army</a>. The 65th Infantry Regiment remained in the north side of the post. The south side was converted into two 300 metres (1,000&#160;ft)  shooting ranges<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> \nThe decision was made to reconstruct all building for the regiment in the north side in concrete <sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> One hundred and ninety buildings were completed, to include the north side of Henry Barracks.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Over 600 men were hired for a period of three years to work in these projects. During this period three large barrack buildings were constructed. The two one company barracks each had its own mess hall and kitchen and was occupied by an infantry company each. The two companies barrack located in the center of the quad occupied the Battalion Headquarters Co. and the Machine Gun Co.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>By 1953, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Army" title="United States Department of the Army">U.S. Department of the Army</a> had reached the conclusion that Henry Barracks would be closed in the near future. A full complement of maintenance personnel composed of professional, technical, and daily laborers were maintained in the Reservation. The growth of three major housing developments is evidence of the economic impact of the Reservation (Reparto Montellano, El Polvorin, Urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n Aponte)<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\nWhile the all-Puerto Rican 65th Infantry regiment would never return to its home base, several other initiatives were undertaken, which had a direct impact on the economic development of the town and the region, one such initiatives was the commissioning of the Caribbean Signal Agency in 1959. Over the coming years several tenants occupied the lands comprised by the Henry Barracks Military Reservation, among them:\n</p>\n<ul><li>In the company size building to the west of the quad, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_National_Guard" title="Puerto Rico National Guard">National Guard</a> had its Officer Training School in 1965 and 1966. It was later moved to <a href="/wiki/Campamento_Santiago" title="Campamento Santiago">Camp Santiago</a> in <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Salinas, Puerto Rico">Salinas</a>. The golf course was used as a helicopter landing strip.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/YMCA" title="YMCA">YMCA</a> <a href="/wiki/Peace_Corps" title="Peace Corps">Cuerpos de Paz</a>, and VESPRA (1965\xe2\x80\x9368) had an Administration Building, a swimming pool, a golf course and three houses, which housed the majors and their families.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Encampment_for_Citizenship" title="Encampment for Citizenship">Encampment for Citizenship</a> held its 1966 six-week encampment in the two-company building in the middle of the quad. One hundred fifty-one young leaders from 56 countries from all over the world meet in Cayey to learn to develop self-government and to perform community development projects.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>The Foundation for Community Development moved to the housing is located in the southeastern part of the Post until 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Thousands of people received training in community development, and leadership during those years.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Cayey is located in a valley surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Cayey" title="Sierra de Cayey">Sierra de Cayey</a>, a branching mountain range of the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a> where the <a href="/wiki/Carite_State_Forest" title="Carite State Forest">Carite Forest Reserve</a> is located, and the main ranges of the Cordillera Central to the west. Because of its location, Cayey is known for its mountains, its cool weather and its misty mornings, especially in winter. During Spanish colonial rule, Spanish soldiers assigned to Puerto Rico were sent to Cayey. Its cool weather resembled the weather of Spain and soldiers could become acclimated to the tropical weather. In winter, it is not unusual for the temperature to drop into the 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Carite_State_Forest" title="Carite State Forest">Carite Forest Reserve</a>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Rivers are: <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Lo%C3%ADza" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza">R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Guavate" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Guavate">R\xc3\xado Guavate</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_J%C3%A1jome" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado J\xc3\xa1jome">R\xc3\xado J\xc3\xa1jome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_la_Plata_(Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio de la Plata (Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado de la Plata</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Maton" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Maton">R\xc3\xado Maton</a>.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate">Climate</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Cayey\'s climate is humid, rainy and mild compared to lower-elevation areas of the island, the area of the town is nearly 1,500 feet (460&#160;m) high, so the climate is subtropical high. In summer average high Temperatures are around 82&#160;\xc2\xb0F (28&#160;\xc2\xb0C) to 88&#160;\xc2\xb0F (31&#160;\xc2\xb0C) and 70&#160;\xc2\xb0F (21&#160;\xc2\xb0C) to 78&#160;\xc2\xb0F (26&#160;\xc2\xb0C) in winter, and low around 68&#160;\xc2\xb0F (20&#160;\xc2\xb0C) to 72&#160;\xc2\xb0F (22&#160;\xc2\xb0C) in summer and 57&#160;\xc2\xb0F (14&#160;\xc2\xb0C) to 63&#160;\xc2\xb0F (17&#160;\xc2\xb0C) in winter. The record maximum temperature is 94&#160;\xc2\xb0F (34&#160;\xc2\xb0C) and minimum 45&#160;\xc2\xb0F (7&#160;\xc2\xb0C). The average annual rainfall is 100&#160;inches (2,540&#160;mm) and maximum rainfall record in 24 hours is 20.87&#160;inches (530&#160;mm) of rain.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Eleutherodactylus_jasperi.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Eleutherodactylus_jasperi.jpg/220px-Eleutherodactylus_jasperi.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Eleutherodactylus_jasperi.jpg/330px-Eleutherodactylus_jasperi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Eleutherodactylus_jasperi.jpg/440px-Eleutherodactylus_jasperi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="499" data-file-height="333" /></a><figcaption> <a href="/wiki/Golden_coqu%C3%AD" title="Golden coqu\xc3\xad">Golden coqu\xc3\xad</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Golden_coqu%C3%AD" title="Golden coqu\xc3\xad">golden coqu\xc3\xad</a> (<i>Eleutherodactylus jasperi</i>; Spanish: <i>coqu\xc3\xad dorado</i>) is a rare and possibly extinct <a href="/wiki/Leptodactylidae" title="Leptodactylidae">leptodactylid</a> frog species endemic to Puerto Rico. Native to the municipality of Caye, golden coqu\xc3\xads have only been found in areas of dense <a href="/wiki/Bromeliaceae" title="Bromeliaceae">bromeliad</a> growth in the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Cayey" title="Sierra de Cayey">Sierra de Cayey</a> between 2,123 and 2,575 feet (647 and 785 meters) above sea level. They get their name from the song the male coquis sing at night. It sounds like "cokee, cokee" so that is why they are called coqui in Spanish. The golden coqui is the smallest of the coqui frogs in Puerto Rico. Mature adult coquis are only roughly the size of a dime. Male coquis are more bright yellow where females tend to be more light yellow and brown. The golden coqui is the only frog species in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">New World</a> known to give birth to live young. These frogs are known around the whole island and are considered a symbol of Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cayey,_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/220px-Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="238" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/330px-Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/440px-Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="1192" /></a><figcaption>Subdivisions of Cayey</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities of Puerto Rico, Cayey is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>. The municipal buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in a barrio referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"el pueblo"</i></span>, near the center of the municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-US2010Census_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US2010Census-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;">\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Beatriz,_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Beatriz, Cayey, Rico">Lapa</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mat%C3%B3n_Abajo,_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Mat\xc3\xb3n Abajo, Cayey, Puerto Rico">Mat\xc3\xb3n Abajo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mat%C3%B3n_Arriba,_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Mat\xc3\xb3n Arriba, Cayey, Puerto Rico">Mat\xc3\xb3n Arriba</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Monte_Llano,_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Monte Llano, href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81vila,_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Pedro \xc3\x81vila, Cayey, Puerto Rico">Pedro \xc3\x81vila</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Piedras,_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Piedras, Cayey, Puerto Rico">Piedras</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Quebrada_Arriba,_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Quebrada Arriba, Cayey, Puerto Rico">Quebrada Arriba</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rinc%C3%B3n,_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Rinc\xc3\xb3n, Cayey, Puerto Rico">Rinc\xc3\xb3n</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sumido,_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Sumido, Cayey, Puerto Cayey, Puerto Rico">Vegas</a></li></ol>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are, in contemporary times, roughly comparable to  <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and subbarrios,<sup id="cite_ref-Census_map_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_map-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span>  (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Cayey: Parcelas Nuevas in Beatriz, Cantera, Sector Jalda Abajo, Cedro, El Coqu\xc3\xad, J\xc3\xa1jome Bajo, La Placita, Saint Thomas, San Crist\xc3\xb3bal, and La Vega.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wordpress.com_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wordpress.com-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Buildings_and_structures">Buildings and structures</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Buildings and structures"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Telemundo_WKAQ_TV_Tower">Telemundo WKAQ TV Tower</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Telemundo WKAQ TV Tower"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Pedro_Montanez.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Estadio_Pedro_Montanez.jpg/220px-Estadio_Pedro_Montanez.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Estadio_Pedro_Montanez.jpg/330px-Estadio_Pedro_Montanez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Estadio_Pedro_Montanez.jpg/440px-Estadio_Pedro_Montanez.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a><figcaption>The new Pedro Monta\xc3\xb1ez Municipal Stadium in Cayey</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Telemundo <a href="/wiki/WKAQ-TV" title="WKAQ-TV">WKAQ-TV</a> Tower, situated at 18\xc2\xb06\'47"N 66\xc2\xb03\'9"W, is a 1,105 feet (336.8&#160;m) tall guyed mast for FM-/TV-broadcasting. It was built in 1971 and it is the second tallest man-made structure of Puerto Rico.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Pedro_Monta\xc3\xb1ez_Stadium"><span id="Pedro_Monta.C3.B1ez_Stadium"></span>Pedro Monta\xc3\xb1ez Stadium</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Pedro Monta\xc3\xb1ez Stadium"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The Pedro Monta\xc3\xb1ez Municipal Stadium in Cayey, proceeded by the first Pedro Monta\xc3\xb1ez Municipal Stadium in Cayey, is the home of the Toritos de Cayey <a href="/wiki/Double-A_(baseball)" title="Double-A (baseball)">Double-A baseball</a> team,<sup id="cite_ref-Isla_News_PR_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Isla_News_PR-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Benigno_Fernandez_Garcia_Middle_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Benigno Fernandez Garcia Middle School">Benigno Fernandez Garcia Jr. High School</a>\'s field day competitions.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Cayey_Pegasus_Broadcasting_WAPA-TV_Tower">Cayey Pegasus Broadcasting WAPA-TV Tower</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Cayey Pegasus Broadcasting WAPA-TV Tower"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The Cayey Pegasus Broadcasting tower, at coordinates 18\xc2\xb06\'33"N and 66\xc2\xb03\'2"W is the third-tallest structure in Puerto Rico. It is a guyed mast owned by Hemisphere Media Group with a height of 1,091 feet (332.5&#160;m), which was built in 1966.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cayey_Road,_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico_circa_1900-1917.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Cayey_Road%2C_Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_circa_1900-1917.jpg/220px-Cayey_Road%2C_Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_circa_1900-1917.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Cayey_Road%2C_Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_circa_1900-1917.jpg/330px-Cayey_Road%2C_Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_circa_1900-1917.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Cayey_Road%2C_Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_circa_1900-1917.jpg/440px-Cayey_Road%2C_Cayey%2C_Puerto_Rico_circa_1900-1917.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1602" data-file-height="1046" /></a><figcaption>View from road in Cayey, circa 1900\xe2\x80\x931917</figcaption></figure><p>Cayey\'s economy was based on growing tobacco, sugarcane and general fruits. Its agricultural economy that evolved starting in the 1950s has diminished considerably. Most of its agricultural products are imported from other islands in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> or <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">mainland United States</a>.\n</p><p>During the first half of the 20th century,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Cayey was basically an agricultural area of small farmers and local haciendas dedicated to the farming of crops for the local market. During the 1920s and 1930s farmers increasingly lost their land to absentee landowners, mostly American companies, that turned to the cultivation of sugarcane and, to a lesser extent, tobacco for export. In the 1950s and 1960s some manufacturing concerns established plants in Cayey taking advantage of tax incentives offered by <a href="/wiki/Operation_Bootstrap" title="Operation Bootstrap">Operation Bootstrap</a>, Puerto Rico\'s industrialization program.\n</p><p>An industrial base, in 1947 Cayey saw the beginning of industrial entrepreneurship. There were three factories in town, the Caribe Flower Co. in the Palo Seco neighborhood, a Baseball Factory in the Toita neighborhood, and a Uniform Factory in the back of the High School. These factories employed mostly females. By 1950 the men that worked agriculture became excess population and began migrating to the United States or join the military. In 1950 with the approval of Fomento Industrial and Operation Bootstrap there was a boom of light factories in Cayey. The Gordonshire Knitting Mill in the Guayama road had twelve large buildings and ran two shifts with more than 1,000 employees, and the Consolidated Cigar Corporation across from the road from the Reparto Montellano neighborhood operated three shifts employing over 2,500 from Cayey and surrounding towns.\n</p><p>There is a <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> bottling location in Cayey.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Crime_in_Cayey">Crime in Cayey</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Crime in Cayey"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cayey_Massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Cayey Massacre">Cayey Massacre</a>, in 1994, took place partly in Cayey.\n</p><p>In August 2019, <a href="/wiki/El_Vocero" title="El Vocero">El Vocero</a> newspaper reported there had been three mass shootings, that year, in Cayey.<sup id="cite_ref-3rd_massacre_in_2019_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3rd_massacre_in_2019-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>To stimulate local tourism, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Tourism_Company" title="Puerto Rico Tourism Company">Puerto Rico Tourism Company</a> launched the <i>Voy Turistiendo</i> ("I\'m Touring") campaign, with a passport book and website. The Cayey page lists the "gastronomic route" in <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Guavate</i></span> barrio,  <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Casa del Cuento y la Historia Cayeyana Ram\xc3\xb3n "Moncho" Gomez</i></span>,  <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Bosque de Pinos</i></span>, and agrotourism at <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Siempre Verde</i></span>, as places of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Cayey is a mountainous municipality with many places of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Landmarks and places of interest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There are seven places in Cayey listed on the US <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-NRHP_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRHP-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Casa de Juana Rodr\xc3\xadguez Morales</i></span></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Church_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_la_Asunci%C3%B3n_of_Cayey" title="Church Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de la Asunci\xc3\xb3n of Cayey">Church Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de la Asunci\xc3\xb3n of Cayey</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Liendre_Bridge" title="La Liendre Bridge">La Liendre Bridge</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Arenas_Bridge" title="Arenas Bridge">Arenas Bridge</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carretera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Carretera Central (Puerto Rico)">Carretera Central</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Mat%C3%B3n_Bridge" title="R\xc3\xado Mat\xc3\xb3n Bridge">R\xc3\xado Mat\xc3\xb3n Bridge</a></li>\n<li>Carretera No. 4 (today <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_15" title="Puerto Rico Highway 15">PR-15</a>) including the Principe Alfonso XII Bridge.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Monumento_Reyes_Magos.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Monumento_Reyes_Magos.jpg/220px-Monumento_Reyes_Magos.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Monumento_Reyes_Magos.jpg/330px-Monumento_Reyes_Magos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Monumento_Reyes_Magos.jpg/440px-Monumento_Reyes_Magos.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="327" /></a><figcaption>Monument to The Three Kings in Guavate</figcaption></figure><p>Other landmarks, landscapes and places of interest are:\n</p><ul><li><a href="/wiki/La_Robleda_Natural_Protected_Area" title="La Robleda Natural Protected Area">La Robleda Protected Natural Area</a></li>\n<li>Comsat Station</li>\n<li>Ram\xc3\xb3n Frade Exhibit<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Brisas De Cayey</li>\n<li>Monumento a Los <a href="/wiki/Biblical_Magi" title="Biblical Magi">Tres Reyes Magos</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carite_State_Forest" title="Carite State Forest">Carite Forest</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carite_Lake" title="Carite Lake">Lago Carite</a></li>\n<li>Escuela de Bellas Artes</li>\n<li>El Sal\xc3\xb3n de La Fama del Deporte</li>\n<li>El Faro del Saber</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Cayey" title="University of Puerto Rico at Cayey">University of Puerto Rico at Cayey</a></li>\n<li>Museo de Arte Pio L\xc3\xb3pez</li>\n<li>Pedro Monta\xc3\xb1ez Municipal Stadium</li>\n<li>Teatro Municipal</li>\n<li>Banda Municipal de Cayey</li>\n<li>Tuna de Cayey</li>\n<li>Casino Real<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Cayey celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in August. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de Asunci\xc3\xb3n</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The festival has featured live performances by well-known artists such as <a href="/wiki/Grupo_Mania" class="mw-redirect" title="Grupo Mania">Grupo Mania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sonora_Ponce%C3%B1a" class="mw-redirect" title="Sonora Ponce\xc3\xb1a">Sonora Ponce\xc3\xb1a</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Alberto_%22El_Canario%22" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Alberto &quot;El Canario&quot;">Jos\xc3\xa9 Alberto "El Canario"</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lalo_Rodriguez" class="mw-redirect" title="Lalo Rodriguez">Lalo Rodriguez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ednita_Nazario" title="Ednita Nazario">Ednita Nazario</a>, and <a href="/wiki/El_Gran_Combo_de_Puerto_Rico" title="El Gran Combo de Puerto Rico">El Gran Combo de Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fiestas_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fiestas-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Cayey include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Regional Fair&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 April</li>\n<li>Torito Olympics&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 April</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1224496135">.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop{border-spacing:1px;border:1px solid races</b></td>\n<td>986</td>\n<td>2.1%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>All municipalities in Puerto Rico are administered by a mayor, elected every four years. The current mayor of Cayey is <a href="/wiki/Rolando_Ort%C3%ADz" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolando Ort\xc3\xadz">Rolando Ort\xc3\xadz</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Democratic Party of Puerto Rico">Popular Democratic Party</a> (PPD). He was elected at the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_general_election,_1996" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican general election, 1996">1996 general elections</a> and has remained in office through all intervening elections since.\n</p><p>The city belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_VI" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district VI">Puerto Rico Senatorial district VI</a>, which is represented by two Senators. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Pereira_Castillo" title="Miguel Pereira Castillo">Miguel Pereira Castillo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angel_M._Rodr%C3%ADguez" class="mw-redirect" title="Angel M. Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Angel M. Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a> were elected as District Senators.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For the 2020 election, Albert Torres Berrios and <a href="/wiki/Gretchen_Hau" title="Gretchen Hau">Gretchen Hau</a> became the District Senators.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2023, Hau stepped down as Senator to become the District 29 Representative.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The flag derives its design and colors from the coat of arms, which is in the center of the flag encircled by a solid black ring. The centered coat of arms and has four triangles pointing to it, two white and two red.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The coat of arms has a three tip mountain, a red bull, and a waving blue stripe representing the abundant water in the zone and also in reverence to the primitive matron of the town of Cayey. The shield is topped with the silver lamb symbol of San Juan of Puerto Rico, and a red book.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_PR-52.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Map_of_PR-52.svg/200px-Map_of_PR-52.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="79" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Map_of_PR-52.svg/300px-Map_of_PR-52.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Map_of_PR-52.svg/400px-Map_of_PR-52.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1259" data-file-height="500" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_52" title="Puerto Rico Highway 52">Puerto Rico Highway 52</a> in red.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Cayey has direct access to <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_52" title="Puerto Rico Highway 52">Puerto Rico Highway 52</a> and its downtown/business area is served by <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_14" title="Puerto Rico Highway 14">Puerto Rico Highway 14</a>, which grants access to <a href="/wiki/Aibonito" class="mw-redirect" title="Aibonito">Aibonito</a> to the west and is the main route to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="University of Puerto Rico">University of Puerto Rico</a> in town, and by <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_15" title="Puerto Rico Highway 15">Puerto Rico Highway 15</a> which grants access to south Cayey and Guayama. <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_1" title="Puerto Rico Highway 1">Puerto Rico Highway 1</a> Bypass runs through the town\'s business area. The municipality has good paved roads and is easily accessible from San Juan, being only 25 miles (40 kilometers) away, as well as from <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a>, being only 38&#160;mi (61&#160;km) away. Due to its proximity to <a href="/wiki/Caguas" class="mw-redirect" title="Caguas">Caguas</a> and easy access via PR-52, Cayey has seen significant growth in the last years.\n</p><p>There are 82 bridges in Cayey many of which travel over <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_la_Plata_(Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio de la Plata (Puerto Rico)">Rio de la Plata</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit 2x" data-file-width="521" data-file-height="355" /></a><figcaption>A twelve-room school in Cayey, c. 1920</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The following schools are in Cayey:<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Benigno Carrion grades: K \xe2\x80\x93 5</li>\n<li>Benigno Fernandez Garcia Middle School grades: 6 \xe2\x80\x93 8</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Harrison_School" title="Benjamin Harrison School">Benjamin Harrison High School</a> grades: 9 \xe2\x80\x93 12</li>\n<li>Centro Adiest. Vocacional Gabriel Bibiloni</li>\n<li>Dr. Ramon Emeterio Betances grades: 6 \xe2\x80\x93 8</li>\n<li>Emerita Leon Elemental grades: PK \xe2\x80\x93 6</li>\n<li>Especializada de Bellas Artes grades: 7 \xe2\x80\x93 12</li>\n<li>Miguel Melendez Mu\xc3\xb1oz grades: 9 \xe2\x80\x93 12</li>\n<li>Salvador Brau Elemental grades: K \xe2\x80\x93 5</li>\n<li>Su Certenejas II grades: K \xe2\x80\x93 8</li>\n<li>Su Eugenio Maria de Hostos grades: K \xe2\x80\x93 8</li>\n<li>Su Gerardo Selles Sola grades: K \xe2\x80\x93 8</li>\n<li>Virginia Vazquez Mendoza grades: K \xe2\x80\x93 5</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Higher_education">Higher education</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cayey,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Higher education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Cayey" title="University of Puerto Rico at Cayey">University of Puerto Rico at Cayey</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ana_G._M%C3%A9ndez_University" title="Ana G. M\xc3\xa9ndez University">University of Turabo</a> at Cayey</li>\n<li>Instituto de Banca y Comercio (satellite campus at Cayey)</li>\n<li>Liberty Technical College</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li>Hospital Menonita de Cayey</li>\n<li>Hospital Municipal de Cayey</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_natives_and_residents">Notable natives and residents</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Ricardo Aponte">Ricardo Aponte</a>, Brigadier General</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Raymond_Arrieta" title="Raymond Arrieta">Raymond Arrieta</a>, comedian</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hiram_Burgos" pro baseball player, the hit that won the 2015 World Series</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Frade" title="Ram\xc3\xb3n Frade">Ram\xc3\xb3n Frade</a>, visual artist/painter</li>\n<li><a
